The accusers are also rarely motivated by money or fame (and in fact, the instant fame is one of the hardest parts of choosing to go forward.)
They also say they‚Äôre motivated more than anything else by the desire for others ‚Äì the public ‚Äì to understand that these men were capable in behaving in XX way, because they believe it says so much about the men's character.
They often say they were triggered by watching their attacker rise in their careers in public office/service. No matter what titles these men hold, to the women, the men will forever be men who inflicted on them the worst kind of pain.
They also painfully fret over the decision to go public. It‚Äôs one thing to confront an accuser who is more or less anonymous, and entirely another to confront someone whose lives unfold in public. Becoming their accuser instantly makes you a public person.
There are remarkable similarities and parallels in the stories of women who come out with public allegations of sexual assault against powerful men.
